--- Commit Message ---
LU-12669 ec: recover data from parity

Restore read data when some OSTs are unavailable from updated parity
codes.

When normal read fails, the read would switch to CIT_EC_RD, and the
ec read inner IO would expand to cover the whole raid set stripes, the
extent lock of the ec_rd would cover the available data OSTs, then
it reads pages from available data objects and parity objects,
calculates and fill in the missing data pages so that the original
outer IO can pick them up and copy to user buffer.

The ec read outer IO is to keep track of the original read position
and count, and the ec read inner IO is to expand the IO to cover the
whole raid set stripes.

lov_ec_read_stripe_pages() would read all pages for one data stripe
across all page positions in a recovery group in a single
cl_io_submit_sync call. And lov_ec_read_parity_stripe() would read
all pages for one parity stripe in a single cl_io_submit_sync call.

Also catch DIO read failure and switch to CIT_EC_RD to recover data
from parity (buffered IO).

Test-Parameters: fortestonly
Test-Parameters: testlist=sanity-ec

Here's summary of my changes:
## Fix Explanation

The compile error was caused by a violation of the C90 standard, which requires all variable declarations to appear at the beginning of a function block before any executable statements.

**The Problem:**
In the `cl_io_rw_init` function, the variable declaration `int rc;` was placed after the `LINVRNT` macro calls and `ENTRY` macro, which are executable statements.

**The Fix:**
I moved the `int rc;` declaration to the very beginning of the function, right after the opening brace and before any other statements. This ensures compliance with C90 standards that the Linux kernel follows.

**Rationale:**
- C90 standard requires variable declarations at the beginning of blocks
- The Linux kernel compilation uses `-Werror=declaration-after-statement` flag to enforce this rule
- Moving the declaration maintains the same functionality while fixing the compilation error
- The change is minimal and doesn't affect the logic flow of the function

This fix resolves the ISO C90 compliance issue while preserving all the functionality introduced by the erasure code recovery patch.

## Summary

**Fix Applied:**
I fixed the C90 compliance error in `lustre/obdclass/cl_io.c` by moving the variable declaration `int rc;` from line 209 to line 207, placing it at the beginning of the function block before any executable statements.

**Rationale:**
The C90 standard requires all variable declarations to appear at the beginning of a block, before any executable statements. The original patch had introduced a variable declaration after the `LINVRNT` macro calls and `ENTRY` macro, which are executable statements. By moving the `int rc;` declaration to the top of the function (right after the opening brace), the code now complies with C90 standards while maintaining the same functionality.

**Changes Made:**
- Moved `int rc;` declaration from after `LINVRNT` and `ENTRY` statements to the beginning of the function block
- No functional changes were made - the variable is still used in the same way
- The fix maintains the original logic and flow of the function

This fix resolves the compilation error: `ISO C90 forbids mixed declarations and code [-Werror=declaration-after-statement]`

Here's summary of my changes:
Good! The `out_of_start:` label at line 2248 is correctly followed by an `if` statement, so it doesn't have the same issue.

## Summary

**Fix Applied:**
I fixed the compile error by adding a semicolon (`;`) after the `out_of_end:` label at line 2279 in `lustre/lov/lov_object.c`.

**Rationale:**
The compile error occurred because in C, labels must be followed by a statement. The `out_of_end:` label was immediately followed by a closing brace `}`, which ends the compound statement but is not itself a statement. By adding a semicolon after the label, I created an empty statement, which satisfies the C language requirement.

This is a common pattern in C code where labels are used for `goto` statements but may not always have meaningful code to execute at that point. The empty statement (`;`) serves as a placeholder that allows the code to compile correctly while maintaining the intended control flow structure.

The fix is minimal and doesn't change the logic of the code - it simply resolves the syntax error that was preventing compilation.

Here's summary of my changes:
## Summary

I have successfully fixed the compile error in the `lov_io_set_range` function in `lustre/lov/lov_object.c`. 

**The Problem:**
The compile error occurred because there was a label `out_of_end:` at the end of a compound statement (right before a closing brace `}`). In C, labels must be followed by a statement, and having a label at the end of a compound statement without any following statement is a syntax error.

**The Fix:**
I added an empty statement (semicolon `;`) after the `out_of_end:` label on line 2284. This satisfies the C language requirement that labels must be followed by a statement.

**Rationale:**
- The fix is minimal and preserves the original intent of the code
- The empty statement after the label is a common C idiom when you need a label at the end of a block
- This maintains the control flow structure where `goto out_of_end;` can still jump to this location
- The fix doesn't change any functionality, just makes the code syntactically correct

The change was:
```c
out_of_end:
}
```

became:
```c
out_of_end:
    ;
}
```

This is a standard solution for this type of C syntax issue and will allow the code to compile successfully.
